Message-ID: <DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE401354751370E@EXVS01.olin.edu>

Hi friends and dealwatchers.

Competition is good. You probably know MediaFire from downloading things off of the internet. They're making a play into the sync'd storage space, which is an interesting move. They're offering 50GB to people who sign up and download their desktop client. Pretty good, and bigger then my already referral plumped Dropbox!

If you want to reward me for bringing you this deal, you can click the following link and we both get an extra gigabyte:
https://mfi.re/?dfkd2xq

Otherwise, you can download the client from MediaFire's website yourself and sign up for an account that way.

Have a wonderful and storage filled break,

-William

Invitation to WECode Conference

 Harvard Women in Computer Science invites you to attend our spring WECode
conference on Saturday and Sunday February 8th (Harvard SEAS campus) and Su=
nday
February 9th (Harvard Innovation Lab). Join us in creating a community of
undergraduate women interested in technology from all over the Boston area.
Attendees may attend for either or both days.  On Saturday, the 8th, there
will be speakers, hands-on workshops, panels, lightning talks and recruitme=
nt
bootcamp led by the WECode sponsors, including Goldman Sachs, Facebook,
Intuit, Google, and Microsoft, as well as smaller companies from the Boston
area. On Sunday, 9th there will be a conversation-style keynote and
hackathon!

Register at  wecode.eventbrite.com. Check out tinyurl.com/wecode for more
info.

Questions? Contact us at harvardwecode at gmail.com

Help us publicize and you can get a chance to win a $50 Amazon gift card! E=
very
referral entered at registration is an entry for the prize, just be sure
they include your email in their registration. More entries means more
chances of winning!

FEATURING:

(Saturday)

Rebecca Parsons - CTO, ThoughtWorks

(Sunday)

Harvard Women in Computer Science invites you to attend our spring WECode c=
onference on Saturday and Sunday February 8th (Harvard SEAS campus) and Sun=
day February 9th (Harvard Innovation Lab). Join us in creating a community =
of undergraduate women interested in technology from all over the Boston ar=
ea. Attendees may attend for either or both days.  On Saturday, the 8th, th=
ere will be speakers, hands-on workshops, panels, lightning talks and recru=
itment bootcamp led by the WECode sponsors, including Goldman Sachs, Facebo=
ok, Intuit, Google, and Microsoft, as well as smaller companies from the Bo=
ston area. On Sunday, 9th there will be a conversation-style keynote and ha=
ckathon!
Register at  wecode.eventbrite.com<http://wecode.eventbrite.com/>. Check ou=
t tinyurl.com/wecode<http://tinyurl.com/wecode> for more info.

Questions? Contact us at harvardwecode at gmail.com<mailto:harvardwecode at gmail=
.com>
Help us publicize and you can get a chance to win a $50 Amazon gift card! E=
very referral entered at registration is an entry for the prize, just be su=
re they include your email in their registration. More entries means more c=
hances of winning!

Hey guys,

TechStars is currently looking for HackStars for their spring and summer
programs. If you are interested in being a developer for an early-stage
company, this is a fantastic opportunity. If you are interested in being a
HackStar in the spring, its a minimum 3 day a week commitment (seniors in
12 credits, this might be something you're interested in), but taking an
LOA would probably be the best route. If you are interested in the summer
program, well then... we are off from school and it could be a summer
internship
=E2=80=8B (:=E2=80=8B


If you are curious about TechStars / working for a startup part-time while
at Olin, feel free to ask me questions. I have a few friends who were
HackStars for the last TechStars program that I'd be happy to put you in
touch with
=E2=80=8Bthem to talk =E2=80=8B
about what the program is like.

Here is the official description below:

*Techstars Hackstar and Associate Program*
Participate in the next Techstars session even if you don't have a startup
team or idea! The Hackstar and Associate program allows experienced
software developers/designers and bd/sales/marketing folks to participate
in Techstars just like a founder.
=E2=80=8B =E2=80=8B
Your participation is invaluable to the startups and will lead to
tremendous opportunities. And it pays. The next Boston session starts Jan
21st, applications already open - to learn more about the program visit
http://www.techstars.com/hackstars

or email rohit at techstars.com.

MHacks is currently the largest hackathon in the world, and will take place
over MLK weekend at the University of Michigan. Come up with a creative
project to hack together over the weekend, or simply take advantage of the
ample mentors from industry to add cool features to a personal project. If
you're interested, there is a bus that will transport you for *free* to and
from MHacks. Sign up for the bus here:
https://docs.google.com/forms/d/186SnXW2qQe6RbL7lwre2bYj8PJkovA9Bfx_GlCeKk6=
c/viewform

From: Brian.Liebson at students.olin.edu (Brian Liebson)
Date: Wed, 15 Jan 2014 13:33:16 -0500
Subject: [Carpediem] Chicago Auditions! Details!
Message-ID: <DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE40135482FEC53@EXVS01.olin.edu>

--_000_DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE40135482FEC53EXVS01oline_
Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

The Babson Players is putting on Chicago as its spring musical!

You've asked for the details and here they are:

There are two days of auditions and each one is different so please read ca=
refully:

Sunday, Jan. 26th
                This day is for anyone interested in auditioning for a majo=
r speaking / singing / acting / dancing role. Please come prepared to sing =
a song of your choice a capella that shows your range and ability to perfor=
m in character. You should also come prepared to do some cold readings from=
 the script, DANCE, and potentially sing from the score. They will likely b=
reak into 3 groups and rotate.

Monday, Jan. 27th
                This day is a dance call, meaning that it is for anyone who=
 is really ONLY interested in dancing. Chicago requires A LOT of strong dan=
cers, so they are accepting dancers who don't want to sing. However, you sh=
ould prepare to learn the words so you can lip synch.


If you have never done theater before, the spring musical is always a bette=
r show to audition for than the fall because The Babson Players tend to acc=
ept way more people in the spring.

If you have any questions, comments, concerns, or even want some audition t=
ips, feel free to contact me.

Brian Liebson

PS If you are planning on auditioning, email me back! A good amount of Olin=
ers have told me they plan to audition, so we should all walk on over toget=
her.

The show dates are April 10-12, and tech week is (obviously) that week righ=
t before.

From: fwop-bounces at lists.olin.edu [mailto:fwop-bounces at lists.olin.edu] On B=
ehalf Of Brian Liebson
Sent: Wednesday, January 15, 2014 10:33 AM
To: 'fwop at lists.olin.edu'; 'carpediem at lists.olin.edu'
Subject: [FWOP] Chicago Auditions! Details!

The Babson Players is putting on Chicago as its spring musical!

You've asked for the details and here they are:

There are two days of auditions and each one is different so please read ca=
refully:

Sunday, Jan. 26th
                This day is for anyone interested in auditioning for a majo=
r speaking / singing / acting / dancing role. Please come prepared to sing =
a song of your choice a capella that shows your range and ability to perfor=
m in character. You should also come prepared to do some cold readings from=
 the script, DANCE, and potentially sing from the score. They will likely b=
reak into 3 groups and rotate.

Monday, Jan. 27th
                This day is a dance call, meaning that it is for anyone who=
 is really ONLY interested in dancing. Chicago requires A LOT of strong dan=
cers, so they are accepting dancers who don't want to sing. However, you sh=
ould prepare to learn the words so you can lip synch.


If you have never done theater before, the spring musical is always a bette=
r show to audition for than the fall because The Babson Players tend to acc=
ept way more people in the spring.

If you have any questions, comments, concerns, or even want some audition t=
ips, feel free to contact me.

Brian Liebson

PS If you are planning on auditioning, email me back! A good amount of Olin=
ers have told me they plan to audition, so we should all walk on over toget=
her.

From: fwop-bounces at lists.olin.edu<mailto:fwop-bounces at lists.olin.edu> [mail=

To: 'fwop at lists.olin.edu'; 'carpediem at lists.olin.edu'
Subject: [FWOP] Chicago Auditions! Details!

The Babson Players is putting on Chicago as its spring musical!

You've asked for the details and here they are:

There are two days of auditions and each one is different so please read ca=
refully:

Sunday, Jan. 26th
                This day is for anyone interested in auditioning for a majo=
r speaking / singing / acting / dancing role. Please come prepared to sing =
a song of your choice a capella that shows your range and ability to perfor=
m in character. You should also come prepared to do some cold readings from=
 the script, DANCE, and potentially sing from the score. They will likely b=
reak into 3 groups and rotate.

Monday, Jan. 27th
                This day is a dance call, meaning that it is for anyone who=
 is really ONLY interested in dancing. Chicago requires A LOT of strong dan=
cers, so they are accepting dancers who don't want to sing. However, you sh=
ould prepare to learn the words so you can lip synch.


If you have never done theater before, the spring musical is always a bette=
r show to audition for than the fall because The Babson Players tend to acc=
ept way more people in the spring.

If you have any questions, comments, concerns, or even want some audition t=
ips, feel free to contact me.

Brian Liebson

PS If you are planning on auditioning, email me back! A good amount of Olin=
ers have told me they plan to audition, so we should all walk on over toget=
her.

Hey guys,

RoughDraft, one of the two student investment teams in Boston, is running
an event on women in tech on the evening of 1/27. This is not designed to
be a complaining session on how few women there are in tech, but to discuss
some of the experiences both women and men in tech have surrounding the
issue.

One of the speakers is an Olin alum: Kelsey Bresman from Technical Machine.
The other speakers are all friends of Olin (all employed Olin students at
some point):

   - Dulcie Madden from Rest Devices
   - Zach Dunn from One Mighty Roar
   - Will Eaton from Startup Institute

If anyone wants to come, I'm helping run the event and will be driving in
that evening (4 spots in my car available).

Let me know asap and sign up on the Eventbrite if you want to attend.
http://rdvsketchwomen.eventbrite.com

Also, if you have any specific questions you'd like to ask, I'm starting to
make a list since I'll be moderating the conversation. Send me any
questions you'd like discussed :)

Jules

Hey there Carpe-ers (and Television-ers (and Breakfast-ers!)!)!

Breakfast club and the newly minted ?television? mailing list are pleased to announce that this Saturday morning, 2014-01-25, there will be the watching of cartoons. With breakfast!

FAQs:
Cartoons?
You know, animated TV shows. We'll watch whatever people are in the mood for, but Scooby Doo and Spongebob are already on the list.

Breakfast?
Waffles. I think.

Morning?
You know, after midnight but before noon. Times haven't exactly been ... discussed.

?Television??
It's a new mailing list! Maybe a club! It's for all things TV, from organizing viewings to discussions, and everything in between. We hope to have some more organized themed events (like 90s Prime Time Night, Saturday Morning Cartoons, The Evolution of the Sitcom, whatever), and some more ad-hoc watchings (when people like you think ?hm... I'm going to watch a few episodes of X? and they want friends!). Join us! Find a new show! Rediscover an old show! Meet some people who share your interests (or obsessions). https://lists.olin.edu/mailman/listinfo/television .

Hey carpe,

My friend's dad is a doctor and wants to make this app. If you're intereste=
d in this job, let me know!

--dan

John told me that you might be interested in building a phone app for our p=
hysicians.  Most people have i-phones, but some have android phones, but we=
 can start with the i-phone app if that is easier.  What I am trying to do =
is set up an app that will take the individual to a set of documents that c=
ould help guide their care during an emergency.  This information would not=
  need to be password protected.  There could be a second tab that would le=
ad the user to non-emergency guidelines, again not password protected. This=
 second area would include a medication formulary that may need to have a s=
earch function.  A third tab would function as a place to list links to sit=
es we commonly use. The final tab would be password protected and would hav=
e more sensitive information such as our company financials etc.

The primary function is to have the emergency protocols readily available, =
and we would be happy to just get that. These are already developed and in =
a pdf format.   If the other three functions cannot be done easily, we can =
add those as an update in the future, or not at all.

Please let me know if you have any additional questions.  I have attached a=
 draft flow diagram of what I am trying to accomplish.  If you have the tim=
e to do this project, that would be great, and you can give me a price prop=
osal.  If you are not interested in doing the work, perhaps you can refer m=
e to someone you know who does this kind of work.  Thank you for your consi=
deration.

Regards,
Rich Colavita

From: dantesantos42 at gmail.com (Dante Santos)

Subject: [Carpediem] Join Olin's Robotic Sailing Team!
Message-ID: <CAFrdoZgNxx7uU6srE0j66tsga69_LtJvUP05A9N8H9E1t=oiDQ@mail.gmail.com>

--001a11363910ec43f604f0878457

Content-Type: text/plain; charset=ISO-8859-1

Want to be part of something bigger than a class project? Join ORS!

This semester we're working on perfecting our *manufacturing
methods*utilizing tips passed down to us by the winners of the
*Americas
Cup*.

We are *revolutionizing robotics* by developing a long-distance *autonomous
vehicle* that requires *no fossil fuel*.

We are revolutionizing sailing by building a smarter boat, *instrumenting* it
so that it can "feel" what a human sailor feels, and sail *better *and *faster
*than a human sailor could.

Come to ORS' first meeting of the semester on Wednesday the 22nd at 8PM.


No sailing experience required.

Incentives:  Snacks, Afternoons on the water, and a trip to San Francisco
this summer.

--001a11363910ec43f004f0878455

Hello Oliners,

As you may know, the Cheerios are Olin's non-auditioned a cappella group. T=
his means that YOU, yes you, can (and should) join us! Our first rehearsal =
of the semester is this Sunday at 3pm in the Jam Room. Coming doesn't commi=
t you to joining; just come and see if it's something you'd like to do! We'=
ll be talking about our plans for the semester, getting song suggestions, a=
nd probably doing some singing!

If you want to sign up to our mailing list, join the Olinsingers list here =
https://lists.olin.edu/mailman/listinfo/olinsingers

Thanks,
Amanda and Jacob (on behalf of The Cheerios)

From Eric.Westman at students.olin.edu  Wed Jan 22 15:28:19 2014
From: Eric.Westman at students.olin.edu (Eric Westman)
Date: Wed, 22 Jan 2014 15:28:19 -0500
Subject: [Carpediem] Summer research experience
Message-ID: <DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE401354879BFB9@EXVS01.olin.edu>

--_000_DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE401354879BFB9EXVS01oline_
Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

FWD:

Cognitive and Autonomous Test Vehicle (CAT Vehicle)
NSF Research Experiences for Undergraduates

Are you interested in programming a car to drive itself this summer? Or lea=
rning how cognitive radio technology is enabling inter-vehicle communicatio=
n? This research experience for undergraduates (REU) permits students to en=
gage with the myriad of applications that are related to autonomous ground =
vehicles.

The intellectual focus of the program includes the following research topic=
s:

* Embedded control systems and algorithms;
* Wireless networks;
* Cognitive radio;
* Sensory data processing and sensor fusion;
* Model-based design for component-based systems;
* Vehicle-to-Vehicle (V2V) and Vehicle-to-Infrastructure (V2I) communicatio=
n; and
* Scalability of algorithms/systems (multi-vehicle, multi-device).

Students need not have existing expertise in these areas, a background suff=
icient for standing as an engineering or computer science/mathematics junio=
r or senior will be sufficient.

Important Information
* Funded by the National Science Foundation
  ** 10 students will be supported for 10 weeks
  ** Stipend of $5,000 over the summer
* Free room, partial food support and $600 travel allowance to Tucson, AZ
* Program Dates: June 5th -- August 12th, 2014
* Hosted by the Electrical and Computer Engineering Department of the Unive=
rsity of Arizona
* Each student will receive letters of recommendation from their REU
  faculty mentors

How to Apply

Visit http://catvehicle.arizona.edu<http://catvehicle.arizona.edu/> for mor=
e details about the program, application instructions, and contact informat=
ion. Application deadline: February 15, 2014 for full consideration (applic=
ations may be considered after this date until all students are selected).

Eligibility

* US Citizen or permanent resident
* Rising junior or senior in engineering, computer science, or mathematics
* Have strong software skills
* GPA of at least 2.9

Preference will be given to students who are interested in research, and co=
nsidering an advanced degree. Members of under-represented groups are stron=
gly encouraged to apply.

Visit our YouTube Playlist to see all 10 experiences from 2013:
http://goo.gl/HM5Hta

 the Gods! Because of this, the MtG club will be hosting a tournament on Sa=
turday, February 22nd at 2pm on the DH Mez. This tournament will be a draft=
 tournament so you don't need to have a deck; we will be making them on the=
 spot! There will be a buy-in of $10 if you want to keep your cards, free t=
o play if you don't. Come and join the fun! Sign up here: http://mrwiki.oli=
n.edu/mrwiki/MagicDraft
-Elliott

Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"

tl;dr: New club where we write songs! 10PM, Thursday nights, EH basement pr=
actice room. iCal attached. If you can't make it to meetings, that's fine, =
but slightly less fun.

ntl;r: I sent an email a month ago gauging interest about a songwriting clu=
b, and I got very positive responses. That means we're moving forward! Here=
's what's going on. (Also I'm working on getting a mailing list set up, so =
email me if you want in on that.)

WHO
Anyone interested in creating music! Any instruments (or lack thereof), any=
 style, any skill level (or lack thereof).

WHAT
Every week, each of us will write a song inspired from some theme! Then on =
Thursdays we'll get together and play/sing/whatever our songs for each othe=
r. (Or don't, if you don't want to.) Then we'll get a new theme, and repeat=
! We'll send the themes out to the list, too.

WHEN
Thursdays, 10PM. (iCal attached.) Yes, I know it conflicts with Baja. There=
 is no time that would have no conflicts. But you don't have to attend meet=
ings to participate!

WHERE
East Hall basement practice room! The one with the Steinway, because it's b=
igger. (Incidentally, I'm also putting up a sheet to reserve times for the =
practice room. If you have any questions/concerns about that, contact me.)

WHY
To make the world more musical! To create rather than consume! To be expres=
sive! For fun! For fame! And most importantly, because songwriting is sexy.

PS, if you can think of a better word than "meeting," I'd love to hear it.

--_000_DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE401354879C275EXVS01oline_

Hello OWLs!

My name is William, and I'm one of the Ninjas for OWL. Awesome!

Tonight, at 7PM, in AC113 We're holding our first RECAP session. These should run for under an hour and are an opportunity to catch up or review on Tuesday's materials, as well as hang with your awesome NINJAs.

This will usually be followed by Office Hours where you can talk with us about any questions you may have about what we've covered or what you have coming up in OWL

You should definitely attend if you can't attend the tuesday session. These will end up being weekly, and if there's demand we'll run a RECAP session on Monday/Sunday to review Friday.

If you have any questions, concerns, or comments, just shoot me an email.

-William

-----Original Message-----
From: breakfast_club-bounces at lists.olin.edu [mailto:breakfast_club-bounces at lists.olin.edu] On Behalf Of Mitchell Cieminski
Sent: Monday, 20 January, 2014 09:12
To: carpediem at lists.olin.edu; television at lists.olin.edu; Breakfast_Club at lists.olin.edu
Subject: [Breakfast_Club] Saturday Morning Cartoons [w]

Hey there Carpe-ers (and Television-ers (and Breakfast-ers!)!)!

Breakfast club and the newly minted "television" mailing list are pleased to announce that this Saturday morning, 2014-01-25, there will be the watching of cartoons. With breakfast!

FAQs:
Cartoons?
You know, animated TV shows. We'll watch whatever people are in the mood for, but Scooby Doo and Spongebob are already on the list.

Breakfast?
Waffles. I think.

Morning?
You know, after midnight but before noon. Times haven't exactly been ... discussed.

"Television"?
It's a new mailing list! Maybe a club! It's for all things TV, from organizing viewings to discussions, and everything in between. We hope to have some more organized themed events (like 90s Prime Time Night, Saturday Morning Cartoons, The Evolution of the Sitcom, whatever), and some more ad-hoc watchings (when people like you think "hm... I'm going to watch a few episodes of X" and they want friends!). Join us! Find a new show! Rediscover an old show! Meet some people who share your interests (or obsessions). https://lists.olin.edu/mailman/listinfo/television .
_______________________________________________
Breakfast_Club mailing list
Breakfast_Club at lists.olin.edu
https://lists.olin.edu/mailman/listinfo/breakfast_club

--_000_DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE4013548A4BC5AEXVS01oline_

Oh yes. It is that time.

I know we are figuring out what to waste our precious time doing this semes=
ter on pithy things like job applications.

Well instead of wasting your time on something useless like that, you can j=
oin the Babson - Wellesley (and as of last semester) - Olin Cheer team!

(Which is actually just the Babson Cheer team comprised of students from al=
l three schools).


This semester we are competing at cheer competitions as well as cheering at=
 Babson home games. We get uniforms and everything.

Tryouts are Feb. 12th at 6PM in the Babson gym.

Anyone can join.

Let me repeat, LITERALLY ANYONE CAN JOIN.

Can you do a backflip? No? You can still join?
No handsprings? Fine also, you can join.
No round-off? No cartwheel? Not even a somersault?
YOU CAN STILL JOIN.


You get to learn cool things like jumping and stunting and stuff as well as=
 getting a good workout.

Even if you don't think you want to, come to tryouts anyways just for funsi=
es.

Any questions? Feel free to ask me!



See you there,

Brian

Hello,

If you had signed up over break to learn MIG/TIG welding, it's time to use =
the Google doc found here<https://docs.google.com/spreadsheet/ccc?key=3D0Aj=
G89TRBXX83dFJwTFFISGZVVk1FRVJTZG5wejBSd0E&usp=3Dsharing> to organize into g=
roups of 2-3, complete the readings and quizzes, and sign up for a training=
 slot with Ethan at the appropriate site (MIG<https://olingmaw.youcanbook.m=
e/> or TIG<https://olingtaw.youcanbook.me/>).

Also, if you haven't yet learned MIG and also want to learn TIG, Ethan woul=
d prefer you learn MIG first. If this is an issue, email him and I'm sure y=
ou can work something out.

Thanks everyone! Happy welding.

Meg Lidrbauch | Class of 2017

From: Ankeet.Mutha at students.olin.edu (Ankeet Mutha)

Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

tl;dr: We are having a competition to not use any eating utensils for a wee=
k.

Let loose your inner caveman this week. How you ask? Sign up on this google=
 doc (https://docs.google.com/spreadsheet/ccc?key=3D0Aro8vXqUxQTXdGNoeHRFcH=
p4WldPdUZNQnRHUmt4dWc&usp=3Dsharing), Pay or venmo me $5, Eat without utens=
ils until before brunch next Sunday. Everyone who succeeds gets to split th=
e pot.
Rules:

1.       You cannot use any utensils (fork, knives, chopsticks, etc.) to pu=
t food into your mouth

2.       You can serve food onto your plate using utensils.

3.       You can use dishes (plates, bowls, mugs, etc.) to hold your food

4.       Any food item should not touch more than one dish. (This prevents =
people from using dishes as utensils)

5.       If you are using food as a utensil, you must at least plan on eati=
ng it.

Email me with any queries. I hope you have a happy caveperson week.



Ankeet

"Pok=E9mon club is just another one of those clubs that has a mailing list =
and is officially recognized but doesn't really do anything...."

[cid:image002.png at 01CF1B55.E6B9A550]

We have a whole slew of activities planned for this upcoming semester!

Join the mailing list<https://lists.olin.edu/mailman/listinfo/pokemon> to k=
now more, but in summary....


1.      Trivia competitions over the list! Once a week, an easy question wi=
ll be sent out, and the first few respondents with the right answer will ge=
t a cheap chocolate prize. Once every two weeks, a hard question will be se=
nt out, and the first respondent with the right answer will get a chocolate=
 prize. Not just cheap chocolate, but something actually good:

[cid:image005.png at 01CF1B55.E6B9A550]

Both of these prizes can be redeemed at the location and time of your choos=
ing.

2.      Movie nights! I have all 16 Pok=E9mon movies and popcorn, and inten=
d to make use of both. Times TBD, but respond if you have suggestions!

3.      Metagaming 101! The one and only official Pok=E9mon tournament, the=
 Video Game Championships, will be coming to Massachusetts in April, and I'=
d love to bring an Olin contingent. As such, I'll start teaching the basics=
. Times TBD, but respond if you have suggestions!

Elizabeth

From Colby.Sato at students.olin.edu  Mon Jan 27 20:11:42 2014
From: Colby.Sato at students.olin.edu (Colby Sato)
Date: Mon, 27 Jan 2014 20:11:42 -0500
Subject: [Carpediem] Volunteer at the Japanese Winter Festival at Wellesley,
 Friday, Feb 14th
Message-ID: <DA80C3E6C10BE94E8FCACEB239C2FEE4013547F277EC@EXVS01.olin.edu>

hey,

Do you like Japanese food? Do you want some for free? Wanna meet new people?

The Japanese club at Wellesley needs assistance serving food. In return, you will get free food and a T-shirt. I volunteered a few years ago, and I still have the shirt. You also get to watch kendo demonstrations, listen to music, and meet people outside of the Olin bubble.

Email Hikari Murayama at: hmurayam at wellesley.edu if you're interested. 
You will need to arrive at 2PM to volunteer. This is the Friday of Candidate's weekend, so nothing should be happening yet. 

Colby

Google NYC has a challenge for you: can you make the web a safer place?



Staying safe online can be a tricky task--for every vulnerability, good or =
bad habits will make you safer or more at risk. Yet the "best practices" ar=
e no mystery; for example, you can see one compilation of these practices a=
t g.co/SecurityGuide2013<http://g.co/SecurityGuide2013>. And there is a gro=
wing philosophy of teaching these practices in fun, interactive ways that g=
et through to people without feeling like work--check out this interactive =
game<https://www.staysecureonline.com/staying-safe-online/quiz/> for one ex=
ample of that philosophy in action.

We invite you to participate in our second annual '24HoursOfGood' Hackathon=
 at Google's NYC office. This year, we will be partnering with Google Ideas=
<http://www.google.com/ideas/about/>, our internal 'Think/Do' tank that wor=
ks on solving large global challenges.

The goal of the hackathon is to develop new, fun, straightforward games tha=
t teach people how to stay safe and secure on the web. In 24 hours, teams w=
ill choose a project from a menu of options, come up with a basic game conc=
ept, and implement a simple prototype that puts the user "in the driver's s=
eat" and makes abstract cybersecurity principles real in a visceral way. Ou=
tputs will be judged based on creativity, usability, polish, and the likeli=
hood of actually changing the habits of the player.



Here's how it will work. Student teams of 4-5 participants will join forces=
 to select a project--you will rank your top three projects a few days befo=
re the event. You'll then come to Google NYC ready to roll, and after dinne=
r and a few API talks, get started on building the solution to your chosen =
problem statement.

Google Engineers and technical staff will be on hand at the hackathon to ge=
t you started, and to help throughout the day and night. To keep you going =
and making the most progress against internet evil-doers, we will be provid=
ing lots of food, drinks, snacks and--most importantly--caffeine.

In addition, the top three winning teams will each receive some great prize=
s (Nexus 7's for first place, Chromecasts for second and third place), as w=
ell as lots of great swag for everyone. We know you want to hack for GOOD, =
so here are the details:



What: 24HoursOfGood Hackathon

Who: Computer science (and related fields) students in teams of 4-5

When: Friday, February 7th at 4pm through Saturday, February 8th at 4pm

Where: Google NYC, 111 8th Avenue (the corner of 8th Ave. and 15th St.)

Why: Hone your hacking skills, do good for the Web and the world, meet fell=
ow tri-state computer scientists... as well as FOOD, FUN, and PRIZES!

If you're interested in participating, please fill out this form<https://do=
cs.google.com/a/google.com/spreadsheet/viewform?usp=3Ddrive_web&formkey=3Dd=
Gl1RE9aWG5JakhHZTBicXlUSlNiU2c6MA#gid=3D0> to sign up by Friday, January 31=
st. Shortly after we confirm teams, Google will contact you to inform you o=
f your project and give you a list of recommended technologies to familiari=
ze yourself with so you can hit the ground running (coding) the day of the =
hackathon.



We're looking forward to seeing you in February to hack for 24HoursOfGood!

Cheers,

Your Google NYC 24HoursOfGood Team

Complete information at: www.24hoursofGood.com<http://www.24hoursofgood.com=
/>



Suzanne Alcott
Corporate Relations Coordinator
781-292-2282 (p)

-------- Original Message --------
Subject: 	Interesting Conversations and Grand Challenge Scholars Program
Date: 	Wed, 29 Jan 2014 01:17:11 -0500
From: 	Yevgeniya Zastavker <Yevgeniya.Zastavker at olin.edu>
To: 	Students - Class of 2014 <Students-Classof2014 at olin.edu>, Students
- Class of 2015 <Students-Classof2015 at olin.edu>, Students - Class of
2016 <Students-Classof2016 at olin.edu>, Students - Class of 2017
<Students-Classof2017 at olin.edu>
CC: 	Yevgeniya Zastavker <Yevgeniya.Zastavker at olin.edu>

Hello, Oliners!!!

As the subject line of this email suggests, I write to you all to remind
you that ?Olin Grand Challenge Scholars Program is alive!? Please, join
us *tomorrow evening, 01/29, at 7 pm* for very /Interesting
Conversations/ about what this Program is, what it does, as well as how
and, most importantly, why you should get involved!I will be there!Food
will be there!Good food will also be there!And, of course, this implies
that you *really* want to be there!

For those of you who would like to know more about the Program prior to
joining /Interesting Conversations/ tomorrow, here is a longer version
of the above paragraph. Olin is one of the Grand Challenge Scholars
Program, GCSP, participating (and founding!) institutions. You've
probably heard some things about the Program or seen some activities on
campus launched by GCSP, /Interesting Conversations /is one of them!

The national GCSPis built on the idea that next generation engineers
should start tackling Grand Challenges while they are still in their
undergraduate programs.To do this, the national Program calls for all
students to fulfill five requirements: (1) pursue a significant project
that aligns with one of the Grand Challenges, while also participating
in (2) Interdisciplinary, (3) Service Learning and (4) Entrepreneurial
activities with an eye toward (5) Global Awareness.

The Olin Program is unique in that our students fulfill these five
requirements by virtue of our curriculum. Therefore, rather than
?checking off the boxes? corresponding to the five aspects above, the
core of the Program is built around the idea of personal growth through
reflection. We encourage students to look back at their time at Olin
(and before) and develop meaningful insights about their overall
professional growth and their future goals. The final deliverable for
Olin GCSPScholars is a reflective portfolio that allows for both
synthesis and analysis of their lived experiences within the framework
of the five GCSPaspects mentioned above. Besides an incredible value
that such a portfolio may have for the students personally, the College
also has a significant interest in students becoming scholars because of
its inaugural role in the national Program. If you are intrigued and
want to learn more right away, check out http://gcsp.olin.edu
<http://gcsp.olin.edu/>.

Bottom line: I will be in ****EH1***tomorrow, Wednesday, 01/29, at 7 pm*
for a conversation and would love you to join me for good dose of
interesting discussions, generous amount of food, and highest quality of
even better food.

Please come by, and let me or Sebastian-James-Julianne-Slater team know
if this time doesn't work for your schedule, so that we can have a
separate conversation with you personally!

Looking forward to seeing you there,

Zhenya on behalf of Olin GCSP

From: Rachel Wang <rswang at mit.edu>

Subject: Olin Foundry @ MakeMIT
To: Juliana Nazare <Juliana.Nazare at students.olin.edu>


Hey Juliana!

I'm Rachel, and undergrad at MIT I'm reaching out to you about a hardware
hackathon I'm helping organize on February 15, 2014. Ian from
Circuiteering/Nonolith Labs told me it'd be a good idea to reach out to the
Foundry about this kind of event. Would you mind forwarding the event
details below to your members? We'd love to have some Olin representation
at MakeMIT--you guys made a good showing at HackMIT and we'd love to see it
again! And if hardware is as up your alley as software, maybe you can win a
prize yourself again!

Thanks!
Rachel
MakeMIT Co-Director

--

*MIT TechX presents*
MakeMIT
*=C2=BB  A revolutionary hardware hackathon*

16* hours*
*200 people*
50* teams*
*$4000+ in prizes*

*phase 1 //* february 15, 8AM - midnight
*phase 2 //* february 22 (invite only)

*=C2=BB **Register today before spots fill up: *http://www.makemit.org

*MakeMIT.* A revolutionary *hardware hackathon* for undergraduate builders,
innovators, and makers - those who are excited and passionate about
designing and building. Compete with your team in a *16-hour prototyping
event* to brainstorm, design, and build whatever products you can come up
with.  Top teams will return the second weekend to make their hacks come
alive in the machine shops. *We have arduinos, soldering irons, 3D
printers, and more.* What are *you* going to make?
 *Questions? Comments? Contact us: team at makemit.org <team at makemit.org>*
*Keep in touch with our latest updates: http://www.facebook.com/makemit
<http://www.facebook.com/makemit>*

bit
[cid:image001.jpg at 01CF1EBD.54C1C130]
Award-winning public radio host David Freudberg will engage with us as we e=
xplore these issues.
What was the carbon footprint of your dinner last night? Agriculture is a h=
uge emitter of greenhouse gases associated with climate change. This is an =
important emerging topic as Americans grapple with recent heat waves, storm=
s and other weather extremes as "the face of global warming".

*         Learn which foods release the highest global-warming emissions an=
d which foods release the lowest

*         Hear stories of people in different communities seeking more 'sus=
tainable food' choices and adapting their diets - especially at college cam=
puses

*         Discover the surprising alignment between climate-friendly foods =
and a healthy die
He'll introduce excerpts of his recent documentary series, broadcast worldw=
ide on NPR.

Tl;dr: $5000. Must be a woman. Deadline is February 7th. Read the attached =
pdf for more info.


Longer: The deadline to apply to the Clare Boothe Luce (CBL) Research Schol=
ars program is on February 7th this year. The CBL program through the Henry=
 Luce Foundation supports women in a year-long research experience. You get=
 $5000 to research over the summer with an advisor on an engineering/scienc=
e project. I highly encourage first-years and sophomores to apply. I was a =
Scholar last year and worked with Lynn Stein on a variety of design project=
s. Read the pdf for more info on the program and how to apply. You can also=
 email me with questions and I'll do my best to answer!
